For example, the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/library/winreg.html#module-winreg" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d9ac6ee54d5c474db9a492315758f93f"><span data-offset-key="d9ac6ee54d5c474db9a492315758f93f:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">winreg</code></span></span></a><span data-key="89cac31e64f241da8b6c020ff106deeb"><span data-offset-key="89cac31e64f241da8b6c020ff106deeb:0"> module is only provided on Windows systems. One particular module deserves some attention: </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/library/sys.html#module-sys" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="75bb172e48b7441d9a0e7e755bf1a96b"><span data-offset-key="75bb172e48b7441d9a0e7e755bf1a96b:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">sys</code></span></span></a><span data-key="bbd836b2a0a641e0bca7cf5b13c182b7"><span data-offset-key="bbd836b2a0a641e0bca7cf5b13c182b7:0">, which is built into every Python interpreter. The variables </span><span data-offset-key="bbd836b2a0a641e0bca7cf5b13c182b7:1">`sys.ps1`</span><span data-offset-key="bbd836b2a0a641e0bca7cf5b13c182b7:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="bbd836b2a0a641e0bca7cf5b13c182b7:3">`sys.ps2`</span><span data-offset-key="bbd836b2a0a641e0bca7cf5b13c182b7:4"> define the strings used as primary and secondary prompts:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> import sys>>> sys.ps1'>>> '>>> sys.ps2'... '>>> sys.ps1 = 'C> 'C> print('Yuck!')Yuck!C>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1b57c1b4a78f48e28fb527cbac00f4b4"><span data-offset-key="1b57c1b4a78f48e28fb527cbac00f4b4:0">These two variables are only defined if the interpreter is in interactive mode.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cc2984f92e6d4e00a75e51192285e869"><span data-offset-key="cc2984f92e6d4e00a75e51192285e869:0">The variable </span><span data-offset-key="cc2984f92e6d4e00a75e51192285e869:1">`sys.path`</span><span data-offset-key="cc2984f92e6d4e00a75e51192285e869:2"> is a list of strings that determines the interpreter’s search path for modules. It is initialized to a default path taken from the environment variable </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/using/cmdline.html#envvar-PYTHONPATH" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="64a0a659f3a64941b05ae8331529776c"><span data-offset-key="64a0a659f3a64941b05ae8331529776c:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">PYTHONPATH</code></span></span></a><span data-key="2c581993e3e740729271c09507929ddc"><span data-offset-key="2c581993e3e740729271c09507929ddc:0">, or from a built-in default if </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/using/cmdline.html#envvar-PYTHONPATH" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="344e709c0a574bfaad70c41f1bae1b6a"><span data-offset-key="344e709c0a574bfaad70c41f1bae1b6a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">PYTHONPATH</code></span></span></a><span data-key="9a36b142462e48a5ba8aabd829d19de8"><span data-offset-key="9a36b142462e48a5ba8aabd829d19de8:0"> is not set. You can modify it using standard list operations:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> import sys>>> sys.path.append('/ufs/guido/lib/python')

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1451943883e34d71babc1574f70f2895"><span data-offset-key="1451943883e34d71babc1574f70f2895:0">6.3. The </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/library/functions.html#dir" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e9254326fbb24daeb8d639bb78568fc3"><span data-offset-key="e9254326fbb24daeb8d639bb78568fc3:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">dir()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="58d269bd863b484ea7f7febde4b104e5"><span data-offset-key="58d269bd863b484ea7f7febde4b104e5:0"> Function</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d00e5d872bc5419088cc762485613592"><span data-offset-key="d00e5d872bc5419088cc762485613592:0">The built-in function </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/library/functions.html#dir" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cd0f604e543c41c18c14d3278d999b67"><span data-offset-key="cd0f604e543c41c18c14d3278d999b67:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">dir()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="477f215890144c57b072b0ca2da8a9be"><span data-offset-key="477f215890144c57b072b0ca2da8a9be:0"> is used to find out which names a module defines. It returns a sorted list of strings:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> import fibo, sys>>> dir(fibo)['__name__', 'fib', 'fib2']>>> dir(sys)  ['__breakpointhook__', '__displayhook__', '__doc__', '__excepthook__', '__interactivehook__', '__loader__', '__name__', '__package__', '__spec__', '__stderr__', '__stdin__', '__stdout__', '__unraisablehook__', '_clear_type_cache', '_current_frames', '_debugmallocstats', '_framework', '_getframe', '_git', '_home', '_xoptions', 'abiflags', 'addaudithook', 'api_version', 'argv', 'audit', 'base_exec_prefix', 'base_prefix', 'breakpointhook', 'builtin_module_names', 'byteorder', 'call_tracing', 'callstats', 'copyright', 'displayhook', 'dont_write_bytecode', 'exc_info', 'excepthook', 'exec_prefix', 'executable', 'exit', 'flags', 'float_info', 'float_repr_style', 'get_asyncgen_hooks', 'get_coroutine_origin_tracking_depth', 'getallocatedblocks', 'getdefaultencoding', 'getdlopenflags', 'getfilesystemencodeerrors', 'getfilesystemencoding', 'getprofile', 'getrecursionlimit', 'getrefcount', 'getsizeof', 'getswitchinterval', 'gettrace', 'hash_info', 'hexversion', 'implementation', 'int_info', 'intern', 'is_finalizing', 'last_traceback', 'last_type', 'last_value', 'maxsize', 'maxunicode', 'meta_path', 'modules', 'path', 'path_hooks', 'path_importer_cache', 'platform', 'prefix', 'ps1', 'ps2', 'pycache_prefix', 'set_asyncgen_hooks', 'set_coroutine_origin_tracking_depth', 'setdlopenflags', 'setprofile', 'setrecursionlimit', 'setswitchinterval', 'settrace', 'stderr', 'stdin', 'stdout', 'thread_info', 'unraisablehook', 'version', 'version_info', 'warnoptions']

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b512a81c7931415c95403dfbc1849087"><span data-offset-key="b512a81c7931415c95403dfbc1849087:0">Without arguments, </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/library/functions.html#dir" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fbe6fa36700b4becafbea77d629b143c"><span data-offset-key="fbe6fa36700b4becafbea77d629b143c:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">dir()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="93e67b88cf8d44d3b1e7a8c09eb06ef5"><span data-offset-key="93e67b88cf8d44d3b1e7a8c09eb06ef5:0"> lists the names you have defined currently:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> a = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]>>> import fibo>>> fib = fibo.fib>>> dir()['__builtins__', '__name__', 'a', 'fib', 'fibo', 'sys']

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="750756a3567445b483005d86105e07ce"><span data-offset-key="750756a3567445b483005d86105e07ce:0">Note that it lists all types of names: variables, modules, functions, etc.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7ce8255e11ae47ad98207d33f92b1a51"><span data-offset-key="7ce8255e11ae47ad98207d33f92b1a51:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/library/functions.html#dir" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f2fdef5d696f42a2be4d21f0f1d5b2c1"><span data-offset-key="f2fdef5d696f42a2be4d21f0f1d5b2c1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">dir()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="149bb913f4304cf2a9bec6c7bd6a9843"><span data-offset-key="149bb913f4304cf2a9bec6c7bd6a9843:0"> does not list the names of built-in functions and variables. If you want a list of those, they are defined in the standard module </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/library/builtins.html#module-builtins" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0a074249dc1c4d68a32cbae5bd26bf13"><span data-offset-key="0a074249dc1c4d68a32cbae5bd26bf13:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">builtins</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b5e7b0d0c4604368804e0c05b57a6078"><span data-offset-key="b5e7b0d0c4604368804e0c05b57a6078:0">:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> import builtins>>> dir(builtins)  ['ArithmeticError', 'AssertionError', 'AttributeError', 'BaseException', 'BlockingIOError', 'BrokenPipeError', 'BufferError', 'BytesWarning', 'ChildProcessError', 'ConnectionAbortedError', 'ConnectionError', 'ConnectionRefusedError', 'ConnectionResetError', 'DeprecationWarning', 'EOFError', 'Ellipsis', 'EnvironmentError', 'Exception', 'False', 'FileExistsError', 'FileNotFoundError', 'FloatingPointError', 'FutureWarning', 'GeneratorExit', 'IOError', 'ImportError', 'ImportWarning', 'IndentationError', 'IndexError', 'InterruptedError', 'IsADirectoryError', 'KeyError', 'KeyboardInterrupt', 'LookupError', 'MemoryError', 'NameError', 'None', 'NotADirectoryError', 'NotImplemented', 'NotImplementedError', 'OSError', 'OverflowError', 'PendingDeprecationWarning', 'PermissionError', 'ProcessLookupError', 'ReferenceError', 'ResourceWarning', 'RuntimeError', 'RuntimeWarning', 'StopIteration', 'SyntaxError', 'SyntaxWarning', 'SystemError', 'SystemExit', 'TabError', 'TimeoutError', 'True', 'TypeError', 'UnboundLocalError', 'UnicodeDecodeError', 'UnicodeEncodeError', 'UnicodeError', 'UnicodeTranslateError', 'UnicodeWarning', 'UserWarning', 'ValueError', 'Warning', 'ZeroDivisionError', '_', '__build_class__', '__debug__', '__doc__', '__import__', '__name__', '__package__', 'abs', 'all', 'any', 'ascii', 'bin', 'bool', 'bytearray', 'bytes', 'callable', 'chr', 'classmethod', 'compile', 'complex', 'copyright', 'credits', 'delattr', 'dict', 'dir', 'divmod', 'enumerate', 'eval', 'exec', 'exit', 'filter', 'float', 'format', 'frozenset', 'getattr', 'globals', 'hasattr', 'hash', 'help', 'hex', 'id', 'input', 'int', 'isinstance', 'issubclass', 'iter', 'len', 'license', 'list', 'locals', 'map', 'max', 'memoryview', 'min', 'next', 'object', 'oct', 'open', 'ord', 'pow', 'print', 'property', 'quit', 'range', 'repr', 'reversed', 'round', 'set', 'setattr', 'slice', 'sorted', 'staticmethod', 'str', 'sum', 'super', 'tuple', 'type', 'vars', 'zip']

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="51cfe8af7760447493ba0eb1ff535daf"><span data-offset-key="51cfe8af7760447493ba0eb1ff535daf:0">6.4. Packages</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cf9ad15619564b1e9ff515b4a8f2ac84"><span data-offset-key="cf9ad15619564b1e9ff515b4a8f2ac84:0">Packages are a way of structuring Python’s module namespace by using “dotted module names”. For example, the module name </span><span data-offset-key="cf9ad15619564b1e9ff515b4a8f2ac84:1">`A.B`</span><span data-offset-key="cf9ad15619564b1e9ff515b4a8f2ac84:2"> designates a submodule named </span><span data-offset-key="cf9ad15619564b1e9ff515b4a8f2ac84:3">`B`</span><span data-offset-key="cf9ad15619564b1e9ff515b4a8f2ac84:4"> in a package named </span><span data-offset-key="cf9ad15619564b1e9ff515b4a8f2ac84:5">`A`</span><span data-offset-key="cf9ad15619564b1e9ff515b4a8f2ac84:6">. Just like the use of modules saves the authors of different modules from having to worry about each other’s global variable names, the use of dotted module names saves the authors of multi-module packages like NumPy or Pillow from having to worry about each other’s module names.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fe1f6129b253485fbe990175003a1d76"><span data-offset-key="fe1f6129b253485fbe990175003a1d76:0">Suppose you want to design a collection of modules (a “package”) for the uniform handling of sound files and sound data. There are many different sound file formats (usually recognized by their extension, for example: </span><span data-offset-key="fe1f6129b253485fbe990175003a1d76:1">`.wav`</span><span data-offset-key="fe1f6129b253485fbe990175003a1d76:2">, </span><span data-offset-key="fe1f6129b253485fbe990175003a1d76:3">`.aiff`</span><span data-offset-key="fe1f6129b253485fbe990175003a1d76:4">, </span><span data-offset-key="fe1f6129b253485fbe990175003a1d76:5">`.au`</span><span data-offset-key="fe1f6129b253485fbe990175003a1d76:6">), so you may need to create and maintain a growing collection of modules for the conversion between the various file formats. There are also many different operations you might want to perform on sound data (such as mixing, adding echo, applying an equalizer function, creating an artificial stereo effect), so in addition you will be writing a never-ending stream of modules to perform these operations. Here’s a possible structure for your package (expressed in terms of a hierarchical filesystem):</span></span></span>

    sound/                          Top-level package      __init__.py               Initialize the sound package      formats/                  Subpackage for file format conversions              __init__.py              wavread.py              wavwrite.py              aiffread.py              aiffwrite.py              auread.py              auwrite.py              ...      effects/                  Subpackage for sound effects              __init__.py              echo.py              surround.py              reverse.py              ...      filters/                  Subpackage for filters              __init__.py              equalizer.py              vocoder.py              karaoke.py              ...

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="07dd1039862348bbbc1afba5d51ac74a"><span data-offset-key="07dd1039862348bbbc1afba5d51ac74a:0">When importing the package, Python searches through the directories on </span><span data-offset-key="07dd1039862348bbbc1afba5d51ac74a:1">`sys.path`</span><span data-offset-key="07dd1039862348bbbc1afba5d51ac74a:2"> looking for the package subdirectory.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c853bed1b0724df6b71fcad1abfb2e4b"><span data-offset-key="c853bed1b0724df6b71fcad1abfb2e4b:0">The </span><span data-offset-key="c853bed1b0724df6b71fcad1abfb2e4b:1">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="c853bed1b0724df6b71fcad1abfb2e4b:2"> files are required to make Python treat directories containing the file as packages. This prevents directories with a common name, such as </span><span data-offset-key="c853bed1b0724df6b71fcad1abfb2e4b:3">`string`</span><span data-offset-key="c853bed1b0724df6b71fcad1abfb2e4b:4">, unintentionally hiding valid modules that occur later on the module search path. In the simplest case, </span><span data-offset-key="c853bed1b0724df6b71fcad1abfb2e4b:5">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="c853bed1b0724df6b71fcad1abfb2e4b:6"> can just be an empty file, but it can also execute initialization code for the package or set the </span><span data-offset-key="c853bed1b0724df6b71fcad1abfb2e4b:7">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="c853bed1b0724df6b71fcad1abfb2e4b:8"> variable, described later.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="24c5bee95ca14336b2bc493f7f2e5a3f"><span data-offset-key="24c5bee95ca14336b2bc493f7f2e5a3f:0">Users of the package can import individual modules from the package, for example:</span></span></span>

    import sound.effects.echo

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="166e6dc11b5447118f89d3a7facf44e5"><span data-offset-key="166e6dc11b5447118f89d3a7facf44e5:0">This loads the submodule </span><span data-offset-key="166e6dc11b5447118f89d3a7facf44e5:1">`sound.effects.echo`</span><span data-offset-key="166e6dc11b5447118f89d3a7facf44e5:2">. It must be referenced with its full name.</span></span></span>

    sound.effects.echo.echofilter(input, output, delay=0.7, atten=4)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a6480a129f444837ab3fc04174175858"><span data-offset-key="a6480a129f444837ab3fc04174175858:0">An alternative way of importing the submodule is:</span></span></span>

    from sound.effects import echo

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1ce445571c594164949aad0a362ee23c"><span data-offset-key="1ce445571c594164949aad0a362ee23c:0">This also loads the submodule </span><span data-offset-key="1ce445571c594164949aad0a362ee23c:1">`echo`</span><span data-offset-key="1ce445571c594164949aad0a362ee23c:2">, and makes it available without its package prefix, so it can be used as follows:</span></span></span>

    echo.echofilter(input, output, delay=0.7, atten=4)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="892e1a28b31b4caa8e2f4c7e868381cb"><span data-offset-key="892e1a28b31b4caa8e2f4c7e868381cb:0">Yet another variation is to import the desired function or variable directly:</span></span></span>

    from sound.effects.echo import echofilter

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e4feb8164c9a4e858aafc29e8398d178"><span data-offset-key="e4feb8164c9a4e858aafc29e8398d178:0">Again, this loads the submodule </span><span data-offset-key="e4feb8164c9a4e858aafc29e8398d178:1">`echo`</span><span data-offset-key="e4feb8164c9a4e858aafc29e8398d178:2">, but this makes its function </span><span data-offset-key="e4feb8164c9a4e858aafc29e8398d178:3">`echofilter()`</span><span data-offset-key="e4feb8164c9a4e858aafc29e8398d178:4"> directly available:</span></span></span>

    echofilter(input, output, delay=0.7, atten=4)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c5068908c0ed483f95f742aa4a4a9aef"><span data-offset-key="c5068908c0ed483f95f742aa4a4a9aef:0">Note that when using </span><span data-offset-key="c5068908c0ed483f95f742aa4a4a9aef:1">`from package import item`</span><span data-offset-key="c5068908c0ed483f95f742aa4a4a9aef:2">, the item can be either a submodule (or subpackage) of the package, or some other name defined in the package, like a function, class or variable. The </span><span data-offset-key="c5068908c0ed483f95f742aa4a4a9aef:3">`import`</span><span data-offset-key="c5068908c0ed483f95f742aa4a4a9aef:4"> statement first tests whether the item is defined in the package; if not, it assumes it is a module and attempts to load it. If it fails to find it, an </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/library/exceptions.html#ImportError" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9f170d30cdb347539c9c439c046f7925"><span data-offset-key="9f170d30cdb347539c9c439c046f7925:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">ImportError</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a1efc5881f5a44dea7d7a069464aa635"><span data-offset-key="a1efc5881f5a44dea7d7a069464aa635:0"> exception is raised.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f00018b5dbc94636aed97c96b8f05be1"><span data-offset-key="f00018b5dbc94636aed97c96b8f05be1:0">Contrarily, when using syntax like </span><span data-offset-key="f00018b5dbc94636aed97c96b8f05be1:1">`import item.subitem.subsubitem`</span><span data-offset-key="f00018b5dbc94636aed97c96b8f05be1:2">, each item except for the last must be a package; the last item can be a module or a package but can’t be a class or function or variable defined in the previous item.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d3603ba8b4ed4a5aa674dbef9d0748ed"><span data-offset-key="d3603ba8b4ed4a5aa674dbef9d0748ed:0">**6.4.1. Importing \* From a Package**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="90c4f5dacfb848db996291ef468cf585"><span data-offset-key="90c4f5dacfb848db996291ef468cf585:0">Now what happens when the user writes </span><span data-offset-key="90c4f5dacfb848db996291ef468cf585:1">`from sound.effects import *`</span><span data-offset-key="90c4f5dacfb848db996291ef468cf585:2">? Ideally, one would hope that this somehow goes out to the filesystem, finds which submodules are present in the package, and imports them all. This could take a long time and importing sub-modules might have unwanted side-effects that should only happen when the sub-module is explicitly imported.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1df0118f9c0845cfbb29b65f8b872594"><span data-offset-key="1df0118f9c0845cfbb29b65f8b872594:0">The only solution is for the package author to provide an explicit index of the package. The </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/reference/simple_stmts.html#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1c0631a74c1345b687d98605009bbd6a"><span data-offset-key="1c0631a74c1345b687d98605009bbd6a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ddaf05895d7e4b3ab482b6da931275f9"><span data-offset-key="ddaf05895d7e4b3ab482b6da931275f9:0"> statement uses the following convention: if a package’s </span><span data-offset-key="ddaf05895d7e4b3ab482b6da931275f9:1">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="ddaf05895d7e4b3ab482b6da931275f9:2"> code defines a list named </span><span data-offset-key="ddaf05895d7e4b3ab482b6da931275f9:3">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="ddaf05895d7e4b3ab482b6da931275f9:4">, it is taken to be the list of module names that should be imported when </span><span data-offset-key="ddaf05895d7e4b3ab482b6da931275f9:5">`from package import *`</span><span data-offset-key="ddaf05895d7e4b3ab482b6da931275f9:6"> is encountered. It is up to the package author to keep this list up-to-date when a new version of the package is released. Package authors may also decide not to support it, if they don’t see a use for importing \* from their package. For example, the file </span><span data-offset-key="ddaf05895d7e4b3ab482b6da931275f9:7">`sound/effects/__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="ddaf05895d7e4b3ab482b6da931275f9:8"> could contain the following code:</span></span></span>

    __all__ = ["echo", "surround", "reverse"]

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="42af783d028a47ef820a6d239d044d85"><span data-offset-key="42af783d028a47ef820a6d239d044d85:0">This would mean that </span><span data-offset-key="42af783d028a47ef820a6d239d044d85:1">`from sound.effects import *`</span><span data-offset-key="42af783d028a47ef820a6d239d044d85:2"> would import the three named submodules of the </span><span data-offset-key="42af783d028a47ef820a6d239d044d85:3">`sound`</span><span data-offset-key="42af783d028a47ef820a6d239d044d85:4"> package.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3"><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:0">If </span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:1">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:2"> is not defined, the statement </span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:3">`from sound.effects import *`</span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:4"> does </span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:5">*not*</span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:6"> import all submodules from the package </span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:7">`sound.effects`</span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:8"> into the current namespace; it only ensures that the package </span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:9">`sound.effects`</span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:10"> has been imported (possibly running any initialization code in </span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:11">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:12">) and then imports whatever names are defined in the package. This includes any names defined (and submodules explicitly loaded) by </span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:13">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="41d48952efd84407a2b520ea96e6a7d3:14">. It also includes any submodules of the package that were explicitly loaded by previous </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/reference/simple_stmts.html#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9473d07e39444c8aaf5a4680d402f5a7"><span data-offset-key="9473d07e39444c8aaf5a4680d402f5a7:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c2c65c51e22940df9a0afb8ef74462e1"><span data-offset-key="c2c65c51e22940df9a0afb8ef74462e1:0"> statements. Consider this code:</span></span></span>

    import sound.effects.echoimport sound.effects.surroundfrom sound.effects import *

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b"><span data-offset-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b:0">In this example, the </span><span data-offset-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b:1">`echo`</span><span data-offset-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b:3">`surround`</span><span data-offset-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b:4"> modules are imported in the current namespace because they are defined in the </span><span data-offset-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b:5">`sound.effects`</span><span data-offset-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b:6"> package when the </span><span data-offset-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b:7">`from...import`</span><span data-offset-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b:8"> statement is executed. (This also works when </span><span data-offset-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b:9">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="cb882572a04c41da88147bde90e2d32b:10"> is defined.)</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="852280886cba4dfb844755969785d32b"><span data-offset-key="852280886cba4dfb844755969785d32b:0">Although certain modules are designed to export only names that follow certain patterns when you use </span><span data-offset-key="852280886cba4dfb844755969785d32b:1">`import *`</span><span data-offset-key="852280886cba4dfb844755969785d32b:2">, it is still considered bad practice in production code.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ac59a7c97f07408b8b2222c2b19f08df"><span data-offset-key="ac59a7c97f07408b8b2222c2b19f08df:0">Remember, there is nothing wrong with using </span><span data-offset-key="ac59a7c97f07408b8b2222c2b19f08df:1">`from package import specific_submodule`</span><span data-offset-key="ac59a7c97f07408b8b2222c2b19f08df:2">! In fact, this is the recommended notation unless the importing module needs to use submodules with the same name from different packages.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="318a486fc5c34a5aa7bf1425f144ddde"><span data-offset-key="318a486fc5c34a5aa7bf1425f144ddde:0">**6.4.2. Intra-package References**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658"><span data-offset-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658:0">When packages are structured into subpackages (as with the </span><span data-offset-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658:1">`sound`</span><span data-offset-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658:2"> package in the example), you can use absolute imports to refer to submodules of siblings packages. For example, if the module </span><span data-offset-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658:3">`sound.filters.vocoder`</span><span data-offset-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658:4"> needs to use the </span><span data-offset-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658:5">`echo`</span><span data-offset-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658:6"> module in the </span><span data-offset-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658:7">`sound.effects`</span><span data-offset-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658:8"> package, it can use </span><span data-offset-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658:9">`from sound.effects import echo`</span><span data-offset-key="0e9475144f2747558d3f36e4bcbc1658:10">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="12a8430102024d84b2b750055408c377"><span data-offset-key="12a8430102024d84b2b750055408c377:0">You can also write relative imports, with the </span><span data-offset-key="12a8430102024d84b2b750055408c377:1">`from module import name`</span><span data-offset-key="12a8430102024d84b2b750055408c377:2"> form of import statement. These imports use leading dots to indicate the current and parent packages involved in the relative import. From the </span><span data-offset-key="12a8430102024d84b2b750055408c377:3">`surround`</span><span data-offset-key="12a8430102024d84b2b750055408c377:4"> module for example, you might use:</span></span></span>

    from . import echofrom .. import formatsfrom ..filters import equalizer

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a60e5c6ea0eb46a981104a1021294226"><span data-offset-key="a60e5c6ea0eb46a981104a1021294226:0">Note that relative imports are based on the name of the current module. Since the name of the main module is always </span><span data-offset-key="a60e5c6ea0eb46a981104a1021294226:1">`"__main__"`</span><span data-offset-key="a60e5c6ea0eb46a981104a1021294226:2">, modules intended for use as the main module of a Python application must always use absolute imports.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c8e0477812cf4f5495265df14fbafb78"><span data-offset-key="c8e0477812cf4f5495265df14fbafb78:0">**6.4.3. Packages in Multiple Directories**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ef73eaeda190477ab7919da5df003f5d"><span data-offset-key="ef73eaeda190477ab7919da5df003f5d:0">Packages support one more special attribute, </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.9/reference/import.html#__path__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="971977dbdcfe47b6b67b0e4aeb5388c1"><span data-offset-key="971977dbdcfe47b6b67b0e4aeb5388c1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">__path__</code></span></span></a><span data-key="2b63a70a7fe640c996b2e712aaf70dae"><span data-offset-key="2b63a70a7fe640c996b2e712aaf70dae:0">. This is initialized to be a list containing the name of the directory holding the package’s </span><span data-offset-key="2b63a70a7fe640c996b2e712aaf70dae:1">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="2b63a70a7fe640c996b2e712aaf70dae:2"> before the code in that file is executed. This variable can be modified; doing so affects future searches for modules and subpackages contained in the package.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="681e2fdb756f47e48d53b68139a6a71f"><span data-offset-key="681e2fdb756f47e48d53b68139a6a71f:0">While this feature is not often needed, it can be used to extend the set of modules found in a package.</span></span></span>

<a href="pdf-downloads.html" class="reset-3c756112--card-6570f064--whiteCard-fff091a4--cardPrevious-56a5e674"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">​</span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">​</span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">​</span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">​</span></span>

<a href="intro-2-python.html#control-flow" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Control Flow</span></span>

<a href="intro-2-python.html#data-structures" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Data Structures</span></span>

<a href="intro-2-python.html#modules" class="reset-3c756112--menuItem-aa02f6ec--menuItemLight-757d5235--menuItemInline-173bdf97--pageTocItem-f4427024"></a>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1--pageTocLinkH2-2294976c">Modules</span></span>
